Authorization Implementation Overview\\n\\nThe RBAC (Role-Based Access Control) authorization system in Kubernetes is implemented across multiple packages and files, orchestrating a sophisticated hierarchy of role resolution, policy enforcement, and escalation prevention. Here's a comprehensive breakdown of the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe RBACAuthorizer (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:50) is the primary authorizer that implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface. Its Authorize method (line 75) evaluates requests against policies by delegating to a RequestToRuleMapper (line 37), which provides the interface for retrieving PolicyRules that apply to users. The authorizer uses an authorizingVisitor pattern to check rules and short-circuit on first allow.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution Hierarchy\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:91) is the concrete implementation of AuthorizationRuleResolver (line 37) that resolves all PolicyRules applicable to a user in a namespace. It implements:\\n- RulesFor (line 118): Returns accumulated PolicyRules for a user\\n- VisitRulesFor (line 179): Visits rules for a user across ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules (line 240): Resolves Role/ClusterRole references from role bindings\\n\\nThe resolver depends on four getter/lister interfaces:\\n- RoleGetter (line 102): Fetches Role objects\\n- RoleBindingLister (line 106): Lists RoleBindings in a namespace\\n- ClusterRoleGetter (line 110): Fetches ClusterRole objects  \\n- ClusterRoleBindingLister (line 114): Lists ClusterRoleBindings cluster-wide\\n\\nIn practice, these are implemented by adapter types in rbac.go (lines 195-225) that wrap informer listers.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go:42) implements SubjectLocator and provides the AllowedSubjects method (line 64) that returns which subjects (users, groups, service accounts) have permissions to perform an action. It traverses both cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings, matching rules against the provided request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Review REST Handler\\n\\nThe REST handler (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go:35) implements a StatelessCreateRest that handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. Its Create method (line 63) validates the request and uses the authorizer to evaluate the decision, then returns a SubjectAccessReviewStatus with allowed/denied/reason fields.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/ with three main modules:\\n\\n1. policy.go: Defines ClusterRoles() (line 197) and ClusterRoleBindings() that provide core system permissions for components like system:kube-scheduler, system:kube-controller-manager. Also includes NodeRules() (line 112) for kubelet permissions.\\n\\n2. namespace_policy.go: Provides NamespaceRoles() and NamespaceRoleBindings() for namespace-scoped default roles in system namespaces (kube-system, kube-public, etc.).\\n\\n3. controller_policy.go: Defines ControllerRoles() and ControllerRoleBindings() for various controller service accounts (replication-controller, horizontal-pod-autoscaler, etc.).\\n\\nThese policies are reconciled at startup via PostStartHook in pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go (line 131).\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe escalation prevention system is implemented through multiple mechanisms:\\n\\n1. escalation_check.go provides three key functions:\\n   - EscalationAllowed (line 32): Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized (line 55): Checks if user has \\\"escalate\\\" verb on role/clusterrole resources\\n   - BindingAuthorized (line 101): Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" verb on the specific role being referenced\\n\\n2. Validation via ConfirmNoEscalation (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53) checks that a user attempting to create/update a role/binding doesn't grant permissions they don't already have.\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage Implementation\\n\\nThe four policy-based storage implementations wrap the standard storage and enforce escalation prevention at the storage layer:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: For Role objects\\n2. pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For RoleBinding objects\\n3. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRole objects (with special handling for aggregationRule requiring cluster-admin)\\n4. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nEach Storage type wraps rest.StandardStorage and intercepts Create and Update operations. They check escalation permissions before delegating to the underlying storage, using either:\\n- EscalationAllowed() for system:masters bypass\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() for explicit escalate permission\\n- BindingAuthorized() for role binding-specific checks\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() to verify the user already possesses the permissions being granted\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\nThe RESTStorageProvider (pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go:61) orchestrates the entire storage setup:\\n1. Creates base storage instances for roles, rolebindings, clusterroles, clusterrolebindings\\n2. Wraps them with policy-based storage implementations\\n3. Creates a DefaultRuleResolver for escalation validation\\n4. Registers the PostStartHook for bootstrap policy reconciliation\\n\\nThe authorizer configuration (pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:123) instantiates the RBACAuthorizer with RoleGetter/RoleBindingLister/ClusterRoleGetter/ClusterRoleBindingLister adapters that fetch data from informers, enabling real-time authorization decisions based on current cluster state.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5632,"cache_read_input_tokens":91071,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5632},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"733fb6e6-9721-469f-ae94-d42f9e2784f0","uuid":"c71c6537-fa87-4739-b87e-9655254182ba"}

Authorization Implementation Overview\\n\\nThe RBAC (Role-Based Access Control) authorization system in Kubernetes is implemented across multiple packages and files, orchestrating a sophisticated hierarchy of role resolution, policy enforcement, and escalation prevention. Here's a comprehensive breakdown of the key components:\\n\\n## Core Authorization Engine\\n\\nThe RBACAuthorizer (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go:50) is the primary authorizer that implements the authorizer.Authorizer interface. Its Authorize method (line 75) evaluates requests against policies by delegating to a RequestToRuleMapper (line 37), which provides the interface for retrieving PolicyRules that apply to users. The authorizer uses an authorizingVisitor pattern to check rules and short-circuit on first allow.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution Hierarchy\\n\\nThe DefaultRuleResolver (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:91) is the concrete implementation of AuthorizationRuleResolver (line 37) that resolves all PolicyRules applicable to a user in a namespace. It implements:\\n- RulesFor (line 118): Returns accumulated PolicyRules for a user\\n- VisitRulesFor (line 179): Visits rules for a user across ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings\\n- GetRoleReferenceRules (line 240): Resolves Role/ClusterRole references from role bindings\\n\\nThe resolver depends on four getter/lister interfaces:\\n- RoleGetter (line 102): Fetches Role objects\\n- RoleBindingLister (line 106): Lists RoleBindings in a namespace\\n- ClusterRoleGetter (line 110): Fetches ClusterRole objects  \\n- ClusterRoleBindingLister (line 114): Lists ClusterRoleBindings cluster-wide\\n\\nIn practice, these are implemented by adapter types in rbac.go (lines 195-225) that wrap informer listers.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\n\\nThe SubjectAccessEvaluator (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go:42) implements SubjectLocator and provides the AllowedSubjects method (line 64) that returns which subjects (users, groups, service accounts) have permissions to perform an action. It traverses both cluster-wide and namespace-scoped role bindings, matching rules against the provided request attributes.\\n\\n## Subject Access Review REST Handler\\n\\nThe REST handler (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go:35) implements a StatelessCreateRest that handles SubjectAccessReview API requests. Its Create method (line 63) validates the request and uses the authorizer to evaluate the decision, then returns a SubjectAccessReviewStatus with allowed/denied/reason fields.\\n\\n## Bootstrap RBAC Policies\\n\\nBootstrap policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/ with three main modules:\\n\\n1. policy.go: Defines ClusterRoles() (line 197) and ClusterRoleBindings() that provide core system permissions for components like system:kube-scheduler, system:kube-controller-manager. Also includes NodeRules() (line 112) for kubelet permissions.\\n\\n2. namespace_policy.go: Provides NamespaceRoles() and NamespaceRoleBindings() for namespace-scoped default roles in system namespaces (kube-system, kube-public, etc.).\\n\\n3. controller_policy.go: Defines ControllerRoles() and ControllerRoleBindings() for various controller service accounts (replication-controller, horizontal-pod-autoscaler, etc.).\\n\\nThese policies are reconciled at startup via PostStartHook in pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go (line 131).\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\n\\nThe escalation prevention system is implemented through multiple mechanisms:\\n\\n1. escalation_check.go provides three key functions:\\n   - EscalationAllowed (line 32): Checks if user is in system:masters group\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized (line 55): Checks if user has \\\"escalate\\\" verb on role/clusterrole resources\\n   - BindingAuthorized (line 101): Checks if user has \\\"bind\\\" verb on the specific role being referenced\\n\\n2. Validation via ConfirmNoEscalation (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:53) checks that a user attempting to create/update a role/binding doesn't grant permissions they don't already have.\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage Implementation\\n\\nThe four policy-based storage implementations wrap the standard storage and enforce escalation prevention at the storage layer:\\n\\n1. pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: For Role objects\\n2. pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For RoleBinding objects\\n3. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRole objects (with special handling for aggregationRule requiring cluster-admin)\\n4. pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: For ClusterRoleBinding objects\\n\\nEach Storage type wraps rest.StandardStorage and intercepts Create and Update operations. They check escalation permissions before delegating to the underlying storage, using either:\\n- EscalationAllowed() for system:masters bypass\\n- RoleEscalationAuthorized() for explicit escalate permission\\n- BindingAuthorized() for role binding-specific checks\\n- ConfirmNoEscalation() to verify the user already possesses the permissions being granted\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\nThe RESTStorageProvider (pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go:61) orchestrates the entire storage setup:\\n1. Creates base storage instances for roles, rolebindings, clusterroles, clusterrolebindings\\n2. Wraps them with policy-based storage implementations\\n3. Creates a DefaultRuleResolver for escalation validation\\n4.
